Linguistic and Metaphysical Critiques
Author discusses linguistic and metaphysical critiques of Aristotelian logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the linguistic critique of al-Shafi'i and the metaphysical critique of the mutakallimun against Aristotelian logic.

Core Idea
Two foundational critiques: language incompatibility and philosophical antagonism.

The first two groups of Islamic thinkers critiqued Aristotelian logic from within Islamic sciences. The scholars of usul al-fiqh, led by al-Shafi'i, argued that Greek logic is based on Greek language characteristics, which differ from Arabic, leading to contradictions when applied to Islamic issues. The scholars of usul al-din (mutakallimun) rejected Aristotelian logic because of its close ties to Aristotelian metaphysics, which contradict Islamic theology. These critiques set the stage for deeper scrutiny of foreign logical systems.

Guided Path
1
Identify the usuliyun and their core claim
The first group, the usuliyun (scholars of usul al-fiqh and usul al-din), are divided into two branches. For usul al-fiqh, al-Shafi'i is the representative. Find the passage where the author states the reason for their critique: that Aristotelian logic is based on the Greek language and contradicts Arabic.
Look for the phrase 'على خصائص اللغة اليونانية' (based on the characteristics of the Greek language).
2
Analyze al-Shafi'i's linguistic argument
Al-Shafi'i argued that applying Greek logic to Islamic research led to contradictions. The author questions whether al-Shafi'i knew Greek or derived this from observation. Note that linguists like Abu Sa'id al-Sirafi and jurists repeated this idea.
Consider the epistemological basis of this critique: is it empirical or theoretical?
3
Examine the mutakallimun's metaphysical objection
The scholars of usul al-din (mutakallimun) rejected Aristotelian logic because of its connection to Aristotelian metaphysics, which is contrary to Islamic theology (ilahiyyat al-muslimin). The author considers this a subtle and sufficient critique.
Identify the key phrase: 'الميتافيزيقا الأرسططاليسية' (Aristotelian metaphysics) and its connection to logic.
4
Compare the two critiques
Both critiques target the cultural and philosophical baggage of Aristotelian logic. One focuses on language, the other on metaphysics. Reflect on how they complement each other in undermining the universal claim of Greek logic.
Which critique do you think is more fundamental? The author hints that the metaphysical critique is 'from the most subtle ideas'.

إذن أمام حركتين - حركة هدم وحركة بناء - ولهاتين الحركتين علل ودوافع قد عرضنا لها من قبل . ولكن علينا الآن أن نستعيدها في إيجاز لكي نصل إلى نتيجتين من أهم النتائج : هما أي حركة من حركات هدم المنطق المختلفة التي ذكرناها تمثل الروح الإسلامية الحقة وأي حركة من الحركات الإنشائية تكون المنهج الإسلامي الصحيح .
أول فريق من مفكري الإسلام تكلمنا عن موقفهم من المنطق الأرسططاليسي هو فريق الأصوليين - أي علماء أصول الفقه وعلماء أصول الدين .
أما علماء أصول الفقه ، فعلل أكبر ممثليهم - وهو الشافعي - السبب الحقيقي لنقد المسلمين لمنطق أرسطو بأن هذا المنطق يقوم كما قلنا - على خصائص اللغة اليونانية - ولغة اليونان مخالفة للغة المسلمين . فلما طبق المنطق اليوناني على الأبحاث الإسلامية أدى هذا التطبيق إلى متناقضات عدة . هل هذا الحكم الذي يضعه الشافعي يقوم على معرفة الشافعي لخصائص اللغتين العربية واليونانية - أو بمعنى آخر - هل كان الشافعي يعرف اليونانية - أم أن الفكرة نشأت لديه حين حاول تطبيق المنطق الأرسططاليسي على مسائل المسلمين فأدى إلى التناقض . قد رأينا من قبل ما ورد في روايات بعض المؤرخين من أن الشافعي كان يعرف اليونانية وفكرة إتصال المنطق الأرسططاليسي باللغة اليونانية وقيامه على خصائصها ومخالفة هذا للمنطق الإسلامي يرددها علماء اللغة كأبي سعيد السيرافي ، كما يرددها الفقهاء .
أما علماء أصول الدين ( المتكلمون ) فقلنا إن العلة في عدم قبولهم للمنطق الأرسططاليسي ، أنهم لم يقبلوا الميتافيزيقا الأرسططاليسية ، لأنها مخالفة لإلهيات المسلمين ، وهذا المنطق الأرسططاليسي وثيق الصلة بالميتافيزيقا وكثير من أصوله تتصل بأصولها ، ولهذا رفضه المتكلمون . وهذه فكرة في الحقيقة من أدق الفكر التي وصل إليها المسلمون وهي كافية لهدم المنطق الأرسططاليسي من وجهة نظر إسلامية .
الفريق الثالث من مفكري الإسلام الذين نقدوا المنطق الأرسططاليسي هم الفقهاء . وأهم ممثلي هذا الفريق هو ابن تيمية . وقد ذكر ابن تيمية العلتين اللتين ذكرهما الأصوليون والمتكلمون من قبل وتوسع فيهما : ثم أضاف إليهما الأسباب الآتية : أولاً . المنطق الأرسططاليسي يقيد الفطرة الإسلامية بقوانين صناعية متكلفة في الحد والإستدلال . ثانياً . اتجاه الإسلام إلى الوفاء بالحاجة الإنسانية المتغيرة بينما المنطق الأرسططاليسي يعتبر قوانينه كلية وثابتة . ثالثاً ـ عدم اشتغال الصحابة والأئمة بهذا المنطق الأرسططاليسي مع توصلهم إلى كل نواحي العلم . وابن تيمية يردد هنا قول ابن الصلاح في تحريم منطق أرسطو .
أما الفريق الرابع الذي بحثنا نقدهم لطرق المعرفة التي تستند إلى النظر أي الصوفية ، فلا نستطيع أن ندخل نقدهم في الاتجاهات التي تمثل نقد علماء المسلمين للمنطق الأرسططاليسي ، لأن الصوفية أنكرت العقل كأداة ، ولا يقبل علماء المسلمون أو متفلسفتهم عقائد الصوفية ولا طريق المعرفة لديهم ويرون أن تجربة ذاتية لا تصلح قاعدة أو منهجاً للحياة وهذا ما يفسر لنا النزاع الذي حدث منذ القرن الثاني الهجري بين الصوفية والفقهاء والصوفية والمتكلمين ، والذي اشتد في بعض العصور بعد ذلك اشتداداً كبيراً .
أما الفريق الخامس فهم العلماء الذين لم يقبلوا منطق أرسطو لأنه طريق نظري يختلف تماماً عن روح أبحاثهم التجريبية .
لدينا إذن أسباب أو علل عبر بها مفكرو الإسلام عن أسباب اتجاههم في نقد المنطق الأرسططاليسي . هذا الإتجاه الذي ساد الدراسات الإسلامية إلى نهاية القرن الخامس أي إلى نهاية العصر الذهبي للعقل الإسلامي الخالص . ولكن هل نستطيع أن نعتبر هذه الأسباب التي ذكرت جوهر هذا الاتجاه في الواقع لا . إنها تشير إليه فقط إشارة عامة ولكنها لا تحدده تحديداً دقيقاً . أما العلة الحقيقية لنقد المسلمين للمنطق الأرسططاليسي فلا نستطيع أن نتبينها من
So we have two movements - a movement of demolition and a movement of construction - and these two movements have causes and motives that we have presented before. But now we must review them briefly in order to reach two of the most important conclusions: which of the various demolition movements of logic that we have mentioned represents the true Islamic spirit, and which of the constructive movements constitutes the correct Islamic methodology.
The first group of Islamic thinkers whose stance on Aristotelian logic we discussed is the group of usuliyun - that is, scholars of usul al-fiqh and scholars of usul al-din.
As for the scholars of usul al-fiqh, the greatest representative among them - al-Shafi'i - explained the real reason for the Muslims' critique of Aristotle's logic: that this logic is based, as we said, on the characteristics of the Greek language, and the language of the Greeks is contrary to the language of the Muslims. When Greek logic was applied to Islamic investigations, this application led to several contradictions. Does this judgment made by al-Shafi'i rest on his knowledge of the characteristics of the Arabic and Greek languages - or in other words, did al-Shafi'i know Greek - or did the idea arise in him when he tried to apply Aristotelian logic to Muslim issues, leading to contradiction? We have seen before what is reported in the accounts of some historians that al-Shafi'i knew Greek, and the idea of the connection of Aristotelian logic to the Greek language and its being based on its characteristics, and its opposition to Islamic logic, is repeated by linguists like Abu Sa'id al-Sirafi, and also by jurists.
As for the scholars of usul al-din (the mutakallimun), we said that the reason for their rejection of Aristotelian logic is that they did not accept Aristotelian metaphysics because it contradicts Islamic theology, and this Aristotelian logic is closely linked to metaphysics and many of its principles are connected to its principles, and for this reason the mutakallimun rejected it. And this idea is in fact among the most subtle ideas reached by Muslims and is sufficient to demolish Aristotelian logic from an Islamic perspective.
The third group of Islamic thinkers who criticized Aristotelian logic are the jurists. The most important representative of this group is Ibn Taymiyya. He mentioned the two reasons mentioned previously by the usuliyun and the mutakallimun and expanded upon them. Then he added the following reasons: First, Aristotelian logic restricts the Islamic fitra with artificial, burdensome industrial laws in definition and inference. Second, Islam's direction is to fulfill changing human needs, while Aristotelian logic considers its laws to be universal and fixed. Third, the Companions and the Imams did not occupy themselves with this Aristotelian logic despite their attainment of all aspects of knowledge. And here Ibn Taymiyya repeats the saying of Ibn al-Salah regarding the prohibition of Aristotle's logic.
As for the fourth group that we examined - their critique of the methods of knowledge based on contemplation, i.e., the Sufis - we cannot include their critique in the trends that represent the critique of Muslim scholars of Aristotelian logic, because the Sufis denied the intellect as a tool, and Muslim scholars or their philosophers do not accept the beliefs of the Sufis nor their path of knowledge, and they see it as a subjective experience that cannot serve as a basis or methodology for life. And this explains to us the conflict that occurred since the second century AH between the Sufis and the jurists, and the Sufis and the mutakallimun, which intensified greatly in some later eras.
As for the fifth group, they are the scientists who did not accept Aristotle's logic because it is a theoretical path completely different from the spirit of their experimental research.
We have thus reasons or causes expressed by Islamic thinkers for their tendency in criticizing Aristotelian logic. This tendency dominated Islamic studies until the end of the fifth century, i.e., until the end of the golden age of pure Islamic reason. But can we consider these reasons mentioned as the essence of this tendency in reality? No. They only point to it in a general indication but do not define it precisely. As for the real reason for the Muslims' critique of Aristotelian logic, we cannot discern it from
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage classifies and analyzes five groups of Islamic thinkers who critiqued Aristotelian logic. The author begins by framing the discussion around two movements: demolition and construction, and aims to identify which demolition movement represents the true Islamic spirit and which constructive movement constitutes the correct Islamic methodology. The first group is the usuliyun, divided into scholars of usul al-fiqh and usul al-din. Regarding usul al-fiqh, the author attributes to al-Shafi'i the argument that Aristotelian logic is based on the characteristics of the Greek language, which differs from Arabic, and its application to Islamic issues led to contradictions. The author questions whether al-Shafi'i knew Greek or derived this from observing contradictions. Linguists like Abu Sa'id al-Sirafi and jurists echoed this. The second group, the mutakallimun, rejected Aristotelian logic because of its close ties to Aristotelian metaphysics, which contradicts Islamic theology. The author considers this a subtle and sufficient critique. The third group is the fuqaha', with Ibn Taymiyya as the main figure. He repeated and expanded the previous two reasons and added three: (1) Aristotelian logic restricts the Islamic fitra with artificial rules in definition and inference; (2) Islam addresses changing human needs while Aristotelian logic claims fixed universal laws; (3) the Companions and early Imams did not use this logic despite their comprehensive knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya also endorsed Ibn al-Salah's verdict on the prohibition of studying Aristotle's logic. The fourth group, the Sufis, is excluded from being a genuine critique of logic because they denied the intellect as a tool, and their subjective experiential path is not accepted by mainstream Muslim scholars or philosophers as a basis for life. The author notes historical conflicts between Sufis and jurists/mutakallimun. The fifth group consists of experimental scientists who rejected logic because it is theoretical and contrary to the empirical spirit of their research. The author concludes that these reasons only point generally to the critical tendency but do not precisely define the real underlying cause of the Muslim critique of Aristotelian logic.

الأصوليون
المتكلمون

خصائص اللغة اليونانية

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the main reason the mutakallimun (Islamic theologians) rejected Aristotelian logic?
A) Because it was based on the Greek language, which differs from Arabic.
B) Because it was closely tied to Aristotelian metaphysics, which contradicted Islamic theology.
C) Because it restricted the Islamic fitra with artificial rules.
D) Because the Companions and Imams did not use it.

Key Takeaway
The linguistic and metaphysical critiques show that Aristotelian logic was not a neutral tool but culturally and philosophically loaded, challenging its universal applicability in Islamic thought.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Commentary Notes
intermediate
8 min
Ibn Taymiyya's Comprehensive Critique
Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Aristotelian logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's three additional critiques of Aristotelian logic beyond those of the usuliyun and mutakallimun.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya argued Aristotelian logic is artificial, rigid, and irrelevant to Islamic practice.

The third group of critics, the fuqaha' (jurists), is represented by Ibn Taymiyya. He expanded upon the linguistic and metaphysical critiques and added three original reasons: Aristotelian logic restricts the Islamic fitra with artificial rules, it fails to address changing human needs, and the early Muslim generations did not use it despite their comprehensive knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya also endorsed Ibn al-Salah's prohibition of studying Aristotle's logic.

Guided Path
1
Recall the previous two critiques
Ibn Taymiyya first acknowledges the linguistic and metaphysical critiques of the usuliyun and mutakallimun. The passage says he 'mentioned the two reasons mentioned previously and expanded upon them.' Keep these in mind as a foundation.
Refer back to the earlier lesson for the linguistic and metaphysical critiques.
2
Identify the three additional reasons
The passage lists three new reasons: (1) Aristotelian logic restricts the Islamic fitra with artificial, burdensome laws in definition and inference. (2) Islam aims to fulfill changing human needs, while Aristotelian logic claims fixed universal laws. (3) The Companions and Imams did not occupy themselves with this logic despite their comprehensive knowledge. Find these in the Arabic.
Look for keywords: 'قيد الفطرة الإسلامية', 'الاحتياجات الإنسانية المتغيرة', 'عدم اشتغال الصحابة والأئمة'.
3
Reflect on the prohibition by Ibn al-Salah
Ibn Taymiyya repeats the saying of Ibn al-Salah regarding the prohibition of studying Aristotle's logic. Consider how this adds a legal dimension to the critique, making it not just an intellectual rejection but a religious ruling.
Think about the implications: if logic is prohibited, it cannot be studied or taught, which would cut off its influence on Islamic thought.
4
Evaluate the relevance of the Companions' practice
The argument from precedent (salaf) is powerful in Islamic thought: the best generations did not use this logic, yet they excelled in all sciences. This suggests that Aristotelian logic is unnecessary for true knowledge.
Consider how this argument might be countered by those who see logic as a tool that can be separated from its Greek context.

Commentary Notes
intermediate
7 min
Marginal Critiques and Conclusion
Author discusses marginal critiques and concludes on the insufficiency of stated reasons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate why the Sufi and scientific critiques are not considered part of the mainstream Islamic critique of Aristotelian logic, and identify the author's claim that the real cause remains unspecified.

Core Idea
The Sufi denial of intellect and the scientists' empirical rejection are peripheral; the true Islamic critique is deeper than stated reasons.

The passage concludes by examining the fourth and fifth groups: the Sufis and the experimental scientists. The author argues that the Sufi critique should be excluded because Sufis deny the intellect itself, which is incompatible with mainstream Islamic thought. The scientific critique is based on the empirical nature of their research conflicting with theoretical logic. Finally, the author suggests that the reasons given only point generally to the critique and do not define its real essence.

Guided Path
1
Examine why the Sufi critique is excluded
The author states that the Sufis denied the intellect (al-‘aql) as a tool, and their criticism is based on subjective experience, not objective reasoning. Because mainstream Muslim scholars and philosophers reject Sufi epistemology, this critique is not considered part of the legitimate scholarly tradition against logic.
Note the phrase 'أنكرت العقل كأداة' (denied the intellect as a tool).
2
Analyze the scientists' empirical objection
The fifth group consists of experimental scientists who rejected Aristotelian logic because it is a purely theoretical path that contradicts the spirit of empirical research (أبحاثهم التجريبية). Their critique is methodological: logic is not suitable for science.
Compare this with the earlier critiques: it focuses on the method, not on language or metaphysics.
3
Reflect on the author's conclusion
The author says that the reasons given by these groups only indicate the critical tendency in a general way but do not define it precisely. The real cause for the Muslims' critique of Aristotelian logic remains unidentified ('لا نستطيع أن نتبينها من'). This leaves an open question for further investigation.
Consider what the real cause might be. Could it be a difference in worldview, epistemology, or something else?

إذن أمام حركتين - حركة هدم وحركة بناء - ولهاتين الحركتين علل ودوافع قد عرضنا لها من قبل . ولكن علينا الآن أن نستعيدها في إيجاز لكي نصل إلى نتيجتين من أهم النتائج : هما أي حركة من حركات هدم المنطق المختلفة التي ذكرناها تمثل الروح الإسلامية الحقة وأي حركة من الحركات الإنشائية تكون المنهج الإسلامي الصحيح .
أول فريق من مفكري الإسلام تكلمنا عن موقفهم من المنطق الأرسططاليسي هو فريق الأصوليين - أي علماء أصول الفقه وعلماء أصول الدين .
أما علماء أصول الفقه ، فعلل أكبر ممثليهم - وهو الشافعي - السبب الحقيقي لنقد المسلمين لمنطق أرسطو بأن هذا المنطق يقوم كما قلنا - على خصائص اللغة اليونانية - ولغة اليونان مخالفة للغة المسلمين . فلما طبق المنطق اليوناني على الأبحاث الإسلامية أدى هذا التطبيق إلى متناقضات عدة . هل هذا الحكم الذي يضعه الشافعي يقوم على معرفة الشافعي لخصائص اللغتين العربية واليونانية - أو بمعنى آخر - هل كان الشافعي يعرف اليونانية - أم أن الفكرة نشأت لديه حين حاول تطبيق المنطق الأرسططاليسي على مسائل المسلمين فأدى إلى التناقض . قد رأينا من قبل ما ورد في روايات بعض المؤرخين من أن الشافعي كان يعرف اليونانية وفكرة إتصال المنطق الأرسططاليسي باللغة اليونانية وقيامه على خصائصها ومخالفة هذا للمنطق الإسلامي يرددها علماء اللغة كأبي سعيد السيرافي ، كما يرددها الفقهاء .
أما علماء أصول الدين ( المتكلمون ) فقلنا إن العلة في عدم قبولهم للمنطق الأرسططاليسي ، أنهم لم يقبلوا الميتافيزيقا الأرسططاليسية ، لأنها مخالفة لإلهيات المسلمين ، وهذا المنطق الأرسططاليسي وثيق الصلة بالميتافيزيقا وكثير من أصوله تتصل بأصولها ، ولهذا رفضه المتكلمون . وهذه فكرة في الحقيقة من أدق الفكر التي وصل إليها المسلمون وهي كافية لهدم المنطق الأرسططاليسي من وجهة نظر إسلامية .
الفريق الثالث من مفكري الإسلام الذين نقدوا المنطق الأرسططاليسي هم الفقهاء . وأهم ممثلي هذا الفريق هو ابن تيمية . وقد ذكر ابن تيمية العلتين اللتين ذكرهما الأصوليون والمتكلمون من قبل وتوسع فيهما : ثم أضاف إليهما الأسباب الآتية : أولاً . المنطق الأرسططاليسي يقيد الفطرة الإسلامية بقوانين صناعية متكلفة في الحد والإستدلال . ثانياً . اتجاه الإسلام إلى الوفاء بالحاجة الإنسانية المتغيرة بينما المنطق الأرسططاليسي يعتبر قوانينه كلية وثابتة . ثالثاً ـ عدم اشتغال الصحابة والأئمة بهذا المنطق الأرسططاليسي مع توصلهم إلى كل نواحي العلم . وابن تيمية يردد هنا قول ابن الصلاح في تحريم منطق أرسطو .
أما الفريق الرابع الذي بحثنا نقدهم لطرق المعرفة التي تستند إلى النظر أي الصوفية ، فلا نستطيع أن ندخل نقدهم في الاتجاهات التي تمثل نقد علماء المسلمين للمنطق الأرسططاليسي ، لأن الصوفية أنكرت العقل كأداة ، ولا يقبل علماء المسلمون أو متفلسفتهم عقائد الصوفية ولا طريق المعرفة لديهم ويرون أن تجربة ذاتية لا تصلح قاعدة أو منهجاً للحياة وهذا ما يفسر لنا النزاع الذي حدث منذ القرن الثاني الهجري بين الصوفية والفقهاء والصوفية والمتكلمين ، والذي اشتد في بعض العصور بعد ذلك اشتداداً كبيراً .
أما الفريق الخامس فهم العلماء الذين لم يقبلوا منطق أرسطو لأنه طريق نظري يختلف تماماً عن روح أبحاثهم التجريبية .
لدينا إذن أسباب أو علل عبر بها مفكرو الإسلام عن أسباب اتجاههم في نقد المنطق الأرسططاليسي . هذا الإتجاه الذي ساد الدراسات الإسلامية إلى نهاية القرن الخامس أي إلى نهاية العصر الذهبي للعقل الإسلامي الخالص . ولكن هل نستطيع أن نعتبر هذه الأسباب التي ذكرت جوهر هذا الاتجاه في الواقع لا . إنها تشير إليه فقط إشارة عامة ولكنها لا تحدده تحديداً دقيقاً . أما العلة الحقيقية لنقد المسلمين للمنطق الأرسططاليسي فلا نستطيع أن نتبينها من
So we have two movements - a movement of demolition and a movement of construction - and these two movements have causes and motives that we have presented before. But now we must review them briefly in order to reach two of the most important conclusions: which of the various demolition movements of logic that we have mentioned represents the true Islamic spirit, and which of the constructive movements constitutes the correct Islamic methodology.
The first group of Islamic thinkers whose stance on Aristotelian logic we discussed is the group of usuliyun - that is, scholars of usul al-fiqh and scholars of usul al-din.
As for the scholars of usul al-fiqh, the greatest representative among them - al-Shafi'i - explained the real reason for the Muslims' critique of Aristotle's logic: that this logic is based, as we said, on the characteristics of the Greek language, and the language of the Greeks is contrary to the language of the Muslims. When Greek logic was applied to Islamic investigations, this application led to several contradictions. Does this judgment made by al-Shafi'i rest on his knowledge of the characteristics of the Arabic and Greek languages - or in other words, did al-Shafi'i know Greek - or did the idea arise in him when he tried to apply Aristotelian logic to Muslim issues, leading to contradiction? We have seen before what is reported in the accounts of some historians that al-Shafi'i knew Greek, and the idea of the connection of Aristotelian logic to the Greek language and its being based on its characteristics, and its opposition to Islamic logic, is repeated by linguists like Abu Sa'id al-Sirafi, and also by jurists.
As for the scholars of usul al-din (the mutakallimun), we said that the reason for their rejection of Aristotelian logic is that they did not accept Aristotelian metaphysics because it contradicts Islamic theology, and this Aristotelian logic is closely linked to metaphysics and many of its principles are connected to its principles, and for this reason the mutakallimun rejected it. And this idea is in fact among the most subtle ideas reached by Muslims and is sufficient to demolish Aristotelian logic from an Islamic perspective.
The third group of Islamic thinkers who criticized Aristotelian logic are the jurists. The most important representative of this group is Ibn Taymiyya. He mentioned the two reasons mentioned previously by the usuliyun and the mutakallimun and expanded upon them. Then he added the following reasons: First, Aristotelian logic restricts the Islamic fitra with artificial, burdensome industrial laws in definition and inference. Second, Islam's direction is to fulfill changing human needs, while Aristotelian logic considers its laws to be universal and fixed. Third, the Companions and the Imams did not occupy themselves with this Aristotelian logic despite their attainment of all aspects of knowledge. And here Ibn Taymiyya repeats the saying of Ibn al-Salah regarding the prohibition of Aristotle's logic.
As for the fourth group that we examined - their critique of the methods of knowledge based on contemplation, i.e., the Sufis - we cannot include their critique in the trends that represent the critique of Muslim scholars of Aristotelian logic, because the Sufis denied the intellect as a tool, and Muslim scholars or their philosophers do not accept the beliefs of the Sufis nor their path of knowledge, and they see it as a subjective experience that cannot serve as a basis or methodology for life. And this explains to us the conflict that occurred since the second century AH between the Sufis and the jurists, and the Sufis and the mutakallimun, which intensified greatly in some later eras.
As for the fifth group, they are the scientists who did not accept Aristotle's logic because it is a theoretical path completely different from the spirit of their experimental research.
We have thus reasons or causes expressed by Islamic thinkers for their tendency in criticizing Aristotelian logic. This tendency dominated Islamic studies until the end of the fifth century, i.e., until the end of the golden age of pure Islamic reason. But can we consider these reasons mentioned as the essence of this tendency in reality? No. They only point to it in a general indication but do not define it precisely. As for the real reason for the Muslims' critique of Aristotelian logic, we cannot discern it from

Commentary
This passage classifies and analyzes five groups of Islamic thinkers who critiqued Aristotelian logic. The author begins by framing the discussion around two movements: demolition and construction, and aims to identify which demolition movement represents the true Islamic spirit and which constructive movement constitutes the correct Islamic methodology. The first group is the usuliyun, divided into scholars of usul al-fiqh and usul al-din. Regarding usul al-fiqh, the author attributes to al-Shafi'i the argument that Aristotelian logic is based on the characteristics of the Greek language, which differs from Arabic, and its application to Islamic issues led to contradictions. The author questions whether al-Shafi'i knew Greek or derived this from observing contradictions. Linguists like Abu Sa'id al-Sirafi and jurists echoed this. The second group, the mutakallimun, rejected Aristotelian logic because of its close ties to Aristotelian metaphysics, which contradicts Islamic theology. The author considers this a subtle and sufficient critique. The third group is the fuqaha', with Ibn Taymiyya as the main figure. He repeated and expanded the previous two reasons and added three: (1) Aristotelian logic restricts the Islamic fitra with artificial rules in definition and inference; (2) Islam addresses changing human needs while Aristotelian logic claims fixed universal laws; (3) the Companions and early Imams did not use this logic despite their comprehensive knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya also endorsed Ibn al-Salah's verdict on the prohibition of studying Aristotle's logic. The fourth group, the Sufis, is excluded from being a genuine critique of logic because they denied the intellect as a tool, and their subjective experiential path is not accepted by mainstream Muslim scholars or philosophers as a basis for life. The author notes historical conflicts between Sufis and jurists/mutakallimun. The fifth group consists of experimental scientists who rejected logic because it is theoretical and contrary to the empirical spirit of their research. The author concludes that these reasons only point generally to the critical tendency but do not precisely define the real underlying cause of the Muslim critique of Aristotelian logic.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the Sufi critique not considered part of the mainstream Islamic critique of Aristotelian logic?
A) Because Sufis rejected logic for linguistic reasons.
B) Because Sufis denied the intellect as a tool.
C) Because Sufis preferred Aristotelian logic but were ignored.
D) Because Sufis had no opinion on logic.

Key Takeaway
The Sufi and scientific critiques are peripheral; the author concludes that the stated reasons only point to the critique, while the real cause of the Muslim rejection of Aristotelian logic remains undefined.
